    Collection of Ancient and Modern Books, Medical Volume 231

    Summer Heat

    Huangdi's Suwen

    Theory of Vital Qi Reaching the Heavens

    Due to summer heat, sweating occurs; when one is agitated, there is panting and loud breathing, while in stillness, there is excessive talking. The body feels like burning charcoal, sweating profusely and dispersing.

    *[Note: The yang evil of heaven harms the yang energy of the body, causing the qi to weaken and sweat to flow. If the pathogenic heat in the qi aspect is severe, it makes the person feel unsettled. The heart governs the pulse, thus the heart feels troubled. The lungs cover the heart, hence agitation leads to panting. If there is stillness without agitation, this pathogen remains in the qi aspect, harming the qi, and as the spirit is weakened, there is excessive talking. The yang evil of heaven harms the yang energy, and with the two yang aspects clashing, the body feels like burning charcoal. The yang heat pathogen resolves through the body's yin fluids, leading to sweating and dispersing.][1p]
    The Great Treatise on the Governance of the Five Constants

    In the Lesser Yang, presiding over heaven, the fire energy descends, while the lung energy ascends. The Great Heat manifests, leading to coughing, sneezing, nasal congestion, oral ulcers, and fluctuations of heat and cold, with swelling. 【Note: In the records of Jin Ping, its organ is the lungs. The ascendance refers to the response to the descending heavenly energy, as one fears being overwhelmed by it. Coughing, sneezing, nasal congestion are all lung diseases. Oral ulcers, fluctuations of heat and cold, and swelling indicate heat conditions.】

    In the Lesser Yin, presiding over heaven, the hot energy descends, while the lung energy ascends. The white metal is utilized, vegetation becomes blighted, leading to wheezing, vomiting, and fluctuations of cold and heat, with sneezing, nasal congestion, and difficulty breathing. The Great Heat, when prevalent, can lead to ulcers and scorching, resembling molten metal and flowing stones. 【Note: The blight of vegetation, and the prevalence of Great Heat, is more intense than in spring and summer. The flow of molten metal and stones indicates excessive heat in autumn and winter.**

    The Great Treatise on the Correct Records of the Six Origins

    In the governance of the Lesser Yin presiding over heaven, the four energies interact, with the humid heat arriving, and heavy rain occurring frequently, alternating between cold and heat. The people suffer from symptoms of cold and heat, dryness in the throat, jaundice, nasal congestion, and excessive thirst. 【Note: In years of excessive conditions, relating to the four chief and guest energies, the humid earth is the master of the atmosphere. The mingling of humid and hot energies causes the arrival of humid heat and heavy rain, leading to alternating cold and heat. The people's symptoms of dry throats and jaundice are all due to the influence of humid heat.】

    In the realm of the Lesser Yang, it is the governor of the scorching heat and the place of heat accumulation, as well as the source of outflows. 【Note: The arrival of energies refers to the conditions of the four seasons influenced by the five movements and six energies, with the Lesser Yang governing the summer heat. The outflow refers to the energy emerging from within to the outside.】[2p]
    On the Importance of True Principles

    The victory of the lesser yin occurs when summer heat arrives, leading to symptoms such as nausea, irritability, abdominal fullness and pain, diarrhea, and a condition known as red dampness. 【Note: The arrival of summer heat coincides with the interaction of the lesser yang energy. Nausea indicates the upward rebellion of yin energy. Irritability reflects the symptoms of yin and yang coldness and heat. Abdominal fullness and diarrhea indicate the presence of cold yin below. The condition of red dampness suggests the excess fire of the heart descending.】
    — Lingshu Classic

    On the Seasonal Dew

    Human beings are affected by the four seasons and the eight winds, which is why there are cold and hot periods. In the cold, the skin tightens and the pores close; in the heat, the skin relaxes and the pores open. 【Note: The infiltration of pathogenic winds and evil qi into people is caused by the fluctuations of their vital energy, which allows for varying depths of invasion, not dependent solely on the opening and closing of cold and heat.】
    — Bian Que’s Difficult Classic

    Heat as a Cause of Heart Disease Related to Just and Disordered Conditions

    How can one recognize the injury caused by summer heat? The presence of foul odors indicates this. Why is that? The heart dominates odors; it manifests as burnt odors if excess heat accumulates within the heart, as fragrant odors when entering the spleen, as fetid smells when affecting the liver, as rotten smells when impacting the kidneys, and as fishy odors when it influences the lungs. Therefore, it is understood that heart disease can result from the damage caused by summer heat, characterized by aversion to foul smells, accompanied by a heated body, irritability, and pain in the heart, with an energetic pulse that is large and scattered. 【Note: The heart's dominion over odors indicates that the heart suffers from summer heat, hence the aversion to foul smells, a symptom that is reflected in the pulse diagnostics, all pertaining to the heart.】
    The injury caused by summer heat relates to just and disordered conditions.[3p]
    [Note: Zheng and xie refer to the sick individual in this text. Heatstroke is considered xie, caused by fire from illness.]
    Shanghan Lun [Han Dynasty, Zhang Ji]

    There are three types of heatstroke.

    For heatstroke from excessive sun, the symptoms include fever, chills, sweating, thirst, and a heavy body. [Note: If there is sweating, chills, and fever without thirst, it indicates a wind attack. If there is sweating, chills, fever, and thirst, it indicates heatstroke, which is treated with Bai Hu decoction plus ginseng according to Jin Gui.]

    For heatstroke due to excessive heat, the symptoms are fever and chills, with body heaviness and pain. The pulse is thin, wiry, and slow. If urination is light and sparse with the hair standing on end, and hands and feet are cold, slight exertion will raise body temperature, with a dry mouth and tongue. If sweating occurs, chills will worsen; if warming needles are applied, fever will increase; if purgatives are used excessively, it will lead to serious dysuria. [Note: There are conditions affecting the surface and the interior, and some that affect both. This indicates an illness affecting both. Fever, chills, heaviness, and pain signify a heatstroke affecting the surface. A thin, wiry pulse indicates vacuity due to heatstroke. Sparse urination and cold extremities suggest insufficient qi in the Taiyang meridian.][4p]
    Those who have slight labor and feel heat are said to exert their yang and become thirsty. If the mouth is dry with the front teeth exposed, this indicates significant heat. If one seems to be gasping and cannot stop, it is due to the dryness of the front teeth. If sweating alleviates exterior evils, then the external yang qi is deficient, leading to severe aversion to cold. If warming needles are used to assist yang, then internal heat attacks, causing an increase in body temperature. If purging is done to eliminate internal heat, then there is internal deficiency and dryness in the bladder, resulting in severe dysuria. Xu said: This condition has no defined treatment; Dongyuan treats it with Qing Shu Yi Qi Decoction, claiming it reveals the ancient secret.

    Those with heat due to solar exposure experience heavy body pain with weak pulses; this results from cold water injuring them in summer, which causes fluid accumulation beneath the skin. The classic states: weak pulse and body heat arise from summer heat damage. Heat with weak pulses indicates thirst. Heavy body pain signifies water retention. In summer, exposure to high heat and water can lead to this condition. The "Jinkui" references a remedy involving the dried gourd stem powder or possibly the Wuling Powder.

    Pulse Text
    By Wang Shuhe of the Jin Dynasty

    Heat-induced weak pulses

    A weak pulse with body heat indicates summer heat damage, resulting in spontaneous sweating, agitation, and palpitations. Fever related to yin deficiency requires early treatment; nourishing and enhancing qi must not be delayed.[5p]
    The Book of Living People [Song Dynasty, Zhu Gong]

    Heat Stroke

    When suffering from heat stroke, if the affliction is deep-rooted and does not heal, the person experiences incessant thirst. The remedy is to take wine-steamed Huanglian pills.

    Heat and Humidity Combined Illness Leading to Damp-Warmth

    If a person has previously suffered from dampness and then succumbs to heat stroke, the combination of damp and heat may manifest as damp-warmth, causing painful coldness in both legs, abdominal distension, excessive sweating from the chest, severe headaches, and delirium. The pulse will feel weak and moist on the Yang side, while the Yin side will be feeble and rapid. The treatment lies within the Taiyin; one must not induce sweating. If sweating occurs, the person will be unable to speak, may have hearing loss, and will no longer feel pain at the site of the affliction, with a bluish complexion. This condition is referred to as severe heat stroke, and if death occurs, it is due to the failure of the physician. The remedy is to use the White Tiger Soup with Cangzhu.

    Summer Season Adjustment Methods

    During the intense heat of summer, one must not wash the hands and face with cold water, as it harms the eyes significantly. The summer season is a time when people's spirits are easily drained; the heart is vigorous while the kidneys are weak. The kidneys transform into water, solidifying in autumn and becoming firm in winter. Therefore, one should be particularly careful with intimate activities and ensure the preservation of one's spirit.

    The Direct Guidelines of the Ren Zhai [Song Dynasty, Yang Dengfu]

    Heat Enters Through the Mouth and Nose

    The heart is interconnected with the stomach. If the stomach's energy is slightly deficient, or due to hunger one encounters heat, the heat toxins enter through the mouth and nose, condensing in the teeth and cheeks, reaching the heart like an echo. Therefore, if one encounters heat, it is advisable to rinse the mouth with water but not swallow it.[6p]
    Heat Stroke

    Heat stroke occurs because the pulse is weak; it is because heat injures the vital energy without harming the physical body. Furthermore, "heat" corresponds to the heavens as heat, to the earth as fire, and to the human body as the heart. Thus, heat particularly injures the heart, causing symptoms such as body heat and headaches, resembling cold diseases, but with coldness in the back and dirt on the face, which distinguishes it. Symptoms include fainting, loss of consciousness, cold extremities, thirst, dry mouth, vomiting, diarrhea, shortness of breath, and a feeling of fullness—all resulting from heat intake.

    Generally, recovering from heat stroke requires avoiding cold water and lying on cold, damp ground, as exposure to cold can be fatal. Instead, one should maintain warmth, applying hot water compresses to the abdomen and the lower dantian, or using hot soil up to the navel, continuing to expel urine. Wait until the person gradually regains consciousness, then slowly administer rice soup and adjust treatment based on symptoms.

    Recently, in the Jiangsu and Zhejiang regions, there have been many incidents of heat stroke leading to convulsions, where the person is unresponsive; such cases are not documented in medical texts. Diagnosing the pulse as floating and weak indicates that floating relates to wind, and weak relates to heat—this is heat stroke compounded by wind, commonly known as "heat wind." If one treats it as a shock or seizure, it often leads to no recovery. In urgent situations, it is advisable to dissolve Su He Xiang pills in warm water and administer them, awaiting slight recovery. Afterward, use a decoction of Huang Lian and Xiang Ru powder combined with Qiang Huo for treatment, and many have responded well to this method.[7p]
    Heatstroke causes profuse sweating, a weak pulse, headache, dry mouth, fatigue, and irritability, sometimes with chills or a fear of heat. Whether the symptoms are exterior or interior, Baihu Decoction is appropriate. If there is severe internal heat, fullness in the abdomen, and a sinking pulse that can be purged, Da Chengqi Decoction is recommended, or San Yi Chengqi Decoction is especially effective.

    For those with heatstroke presenting with spontaneous sweating and a weak pulse, the heat injures qi, causing excessive sweating; hence, the pulse cannot be strong and instead becomes weak.

    Symptoms of heatstroke include body heat, headache, chills in the back, sallow complexion, spontaneous sweating, irritability, extreme thirst, dry mouth, fatigue without body pain, sometimes with chills or fear of heat, a weak pulse, and regardless of exterior or interior symptoms, Baihu Decoction is suitable. In summer, catching a cold often leads to fever and thirst; thus, Wuling Powder, Guiling Ganlu Drink, Huanglian Xiangru Drink, or Shuangjie Powder can be used. If internal heat is severe, abdominal fullness, and a sunk pulse can be purged, Da Chengqi Decoction should be applied, or San Yi Chengqi Decoction is particularly good. For those in a half-exterior, half-interior condition, Xiao Chaihu Decoction, Liangge Powder, or Tianshui Powder can be used.

    Movement and stillness are different.

    In cases of movement leading to heat injury, the heart fire intensifies and lung qi is fully depleted, resulting in body heat and a bounding pulse. When movement produces excess fire, it injures qi. Baihu Decoction with ginseng is the main treatment. Those in hard labor often acquire this condition; it is essential to be aware of it.

    In cases of stillness leading to heat injury, fire occupies the position of metal, lung qi moves to the exterior, resulting in chills and a rapid, deep pulse. When stillness results in excess dampness, the body feels heavy. Baihu Decoction with Atractylodes is the primary treatment. Those in a state of comfort frequently suffer from this; it is important to be aware.[8p]
    Distinction between Heat Stroke and Excess Heat

    Jie Gu said: Heat stroke is caused by remaining still, while excess heat is caused by movement. Heat stroke is a yin condition, and excess heat is a yang condition. If one avoids the heat in a deep hall or grand building and falls ill, it is called heat stroke. The symptoms will include headache, aversion to cold, a stiff body, joint pain, irritability, and extremely hot skin without sweat, due to being restrained by the yin cold of the room, preventing the body's yang energy from spreading out; Da Shun San is the remedy for this. However, if a traveler or farmer labors in the midday sun, it is called excess heat. The symptoms will include severe headache, agitation, feeling overheated, and extremely hot skin, with great thirst and copious sweating; one will lack the energy to move, which is an external injury to the lung energy from the intense heat, and the remedy is Cang Zhu Bai Hu Tang.

    I propose that heat-related illnesses are a result of summer's decree; fire flows between heaven and earth, and people may labor or suffer from hunger, resulting in depleted vital energy that is insufficient to withstand the extreme decree of heaven, leading to injury and illness known as heat stroke or excess heat; in essence, they are the same. Why, then, distinguish them by movement and stillness? Indeed, heat stroke often occurs in laborers; the exertion makes them weak, and weakness allows pathogens to enter, causing illness. If one is not weak, then despite the extreme decree of heaven, there would be no way to harm them. Those who avoid the heat in deep halls and suffer from symptoms like headaches and aversion to cold are simply suffering from exposure to cold, and should not be labeled as experiencing heat stroke.[9p]
    The distress caused by heat and the body feeling overly warm is not due to summer heat; rather, it is because the yang energy within the body is restrained by yin and cold. Since it is not summer heat, how can it be called heatstroke? If one wishes to treat it, then a gentle, warming formula can be used for dispersion. The Great Shun Powder is the main formula, with licorice as the most prominent ingredient, followed by dried ginger and almonds. Except for the cinnamon, the other three ingredients are all toasted, and this was originally intended to address the effects of overheating from excessive drinking, causing the spleen and stomach to be damp, leading to vomiting, where food and fluids become indistinct, and the organs are out of harmony. Thus, licorice and dried ginger are both roasted to ensure they are well-prepared. The use of cinnamon instead of cinnamon twig is meant to provide warming properties. The inclusion of almonds serves merely to help descend the qi. However, if this medicine is used to treat a static condition, I fear it cannot release the exterior and might actually increase internal distress. In today's society, many lack understanding and often assert that in the summer months, the internal yin energy is present, and the Great Shun Powder is a necessary medicine. Alas! Is this not a serious mistake? Yin energy is not cold energy; indeed, in summer, the yang energy disperses outward, while yin energy remains within. Is it appropriate to perceive yin energy as cold and use warming medicines against it? If yin were truly cold, why would water be consumed in summer? While the苍朮白虎汤 (Cang Zhu Bai Hu Decoction) is indeed suitable, should it be viewed as a universally applicable remedy? It must be combined with treatments for heat, using them according to the symptoms observed, for then it would be reasonable. As for what is called a diagnosis from a static condition, even during the summer months, if it is not a case of summer illness, it should be differentiated and not allow future generations to confuse the similar yet different signs.[10p]
    On Heat Injury to Stomach Qi

    The "Treatise on Stabbing Will" states: Qi deficiency causes body heat, which results from summer heat injury. Heat damages Qi. The "Treatise on Atrophy" mentions: If one travels a great distance and becomes tired, encountering great heat and thirst, then thirst will deplete Yang Qi. If Yang Qi is depleted, heat will abandon the kidneys, which are the water organ. If water cannot overcome fire, bones will become dry and marrow will be deficient, leading to weakness in the legs and resulting in bone atrophy. Thus, the "Lower Classics" state: Bone atrophy arises from great heat. This form of damp-heat leads to atrophy, causing the bones to lack strength. Therefore, we treat atrophy primarily with Yangming.

    During the long summer, damp-heat prevails and it is intensely oppressive. When people are affected by this, they often experience fatigue in their limbs, diminished spirit, reluctance to move, chest fullness, shortness of breath, heavy limbs and joints, or high fever with wheezing, a hot and irritable body, distension below the heart, yellow and scant urine, frequent and loose bowel movements, possibly with diarrhea resembling yellow liquid, or resembling thin rice soup. One may feel thirsty or not, lack appetite, sweat excessively and feel heavy, or sweat less—indicating blood is affected first while Qi remains unwell. The pulse presents as flooding and relaxed.[11p]
    If humidity collides, it must be treated with a gradual approach. Although the ailments may interchange and heal slowly, the cause is the same with heat and dampness in summer; therefore, it is advisable to treat it with drying and clearing agents. The Internal Classic states: "Yang Qi protects the exterior and solidifies it; when it is insufficient, Qi leaks." Now, as summer pathogens disturb the protective layer, thus causing heat and sweating, the remedy is to use astragalus, ginseng, and licorice to tonify and enhance Qi. The peel of tangerine, and the body of angelica, sweet, spicy, and slightly warm, nourish the stomach Qi and harmonize the blood vessels, serving as assistants. Atractylodes, white atractylodes, and poria promote diuresis to eliminate dampness; caulis cum propriety and kudzu root, bitter, sweet, and neutral, effectively relieve muscle heat.

    Additionally, when dampness prevails, digestion is affected, leading to bloating; thus, roasted malt, sweet and spicy, and the sweet warm flavor of green tangerine promote digestion and alleviate Qi stagnation. The kidneys dislike dryness, so urgent will require spicy foods to moisten, thus using bitter, spicy, and cold rhubarb to balance heat and supplement fluids. Those with deficiency should nourish their source of transformation using five-flavored fruit and ophiopogon, which are sour, sweet, and slightly cold, to counter the damage from summer heat throughout the metal phase. This is named the Clear Summer Heat and Qi Enhancing Decoction. Summer sickness arises from irregular diet and overexertion, which, over time, weakens the spleen and stomach, resulting in illness during the hot summer days.[12p]
    Managing Heat According to Seasonal Changes

    During the extremely hot months of summer, if one is harmed by cold and hard substances, warm medicines should be used. For instance, the herb Mu Xiang combined with Jian Wan will treat this condition. It is necessary to add a small amount of San Huang Wan, as it is said that the seasonal environment should not be violated; thus, cold medicines are added to align with the season. If harmed by heat, then only San Huang Wan should be used. What does this mean? San Huang Wan is a warm medicine.

    If the spleen and stomach are weak, there will certainly be insufficient upward energy. When encountering the intense heat of summer, it can damage vital energy, leading to lethargy and a desire to lie down. The limbs may become weak, and there is a lack of spirit, with the feet feeling limp. In the face of early morning or evening cold, after the sun is high and the Yang energy is strong, heat rises like fire, resulting in a lack of both Yin and Yang energy and blood. This might cause either heat syncope due to Yin deficiency or cold syncope due to Qi deficiency. Patients may struggle to taste food, feel a burning sensation in their eyes, see little clearly, experience frequent urination, and have difficult and constipated bowel movements. There may also be pain in the stomach and heart area, pain or cramping on both sides, a feeling of tightness around the navel, sharp pain akin to a knife when it becomes acute, a feeling of fullness in the abdomen, a sensation of blockage in the chest, occasional nausea, or phlegm cough; frothy white foam may form in the mouth, with a stiff tongue. Pain in the lower back and along the shoulder blades may occur, headaches may be episodic, appetite may diminish or a sense of fullness may arise immediately upon eating, showing no desire for food, along with particularly profuse sweating.

    If Yin energy stands above the skin and hair, this is due to the heat of the weather exacerbating the original affliction, leading to the heat of the large intestine and lungs being affected. One must first help to boost the vital energy and address the insufficiency of the metal elements (geng and xin). The formula Huang Qi Ren Shen Decoction is advisable for this.[13p]
    If there is stagnation and discomfort in the heart, add two or three fen of huanglian; if there is pain in the chest and stomach, reduce cold medicines and add five fen of cardamom seed; for pain or cramping in the flanks, add two or three fen of chaihu; if there is headache with burning in the eyes, add two or three fen of huanglian and three fen of chuanxiong; if headaches are accompanied by unclear vision, with upper obstruction and heat, add three fen each of manjingzi and chuanxiong, two fen each of dry rehmannia and liangchen, and one fen of xiexin; if shortness of breath causes a feeling of drowsiness and fatigue, add nine pieces of wuweizi; if the stools are dry and difficult to pass, leading to reduced appetite and blood being blocked with heat, add five fen each of danggui, shengdi, and mazi ren, and three peeled peach kernels ground separately; if the stools are passing well, do not take those added medicines again; if the stools are still delayed, do not use other medicines but add five fen of softened dahuang; if they remain unwell, it is not that blood is stagnant but heat causing wind, therefore the patient will show signs of wind disease; one cannot add blood medicines again, only routinely take huangqi and ginseng decoction, using five qian each of qianhu and fangfeng, chewing the two herbs, steep them in four bowls of water until reduced to one bowl, strain out the residues, and take it on an empty stomach, and the stools will certainly pass freely. One dose will suffice.[14p]
    If there is stagnation of qi in the chest, add one or two parts of fresh aromatic green peel, and double the amount of cured tangerine peel to expel its evil qi. This condition is fundamentally due to insufficient original qi; thus, one should supplement original qi and not drain it. If the qi stagnation is too severe or if the tonics are excessive, and the patient has worries and oppressed feelings beneath the heart, add two or three parts of mu xiang (saussurea) and sha ren (amomum) as well as two parts of white cardamom to be cooked with the main herbs. If there are abdominal pains without aversion to cold, add five parts of white peony root and two parts of yellow qin, while reducing the amount of schisandra.

    Xu said: This refers to heat from summer, with similar symptoms. In the winter, cold injury manifests in different forms. The former injures the qi due to heat, while the latter damages the form due to cold. If the original qi is severely deficient and the condition is not addressed in time, it can be as harmful as cold damage with its hidden toxins. Therefore, Dongyuan's teachings illuminate this case, opening the eyes of future generations, and it is advisable to consider it together with Wei Men’s insights.

    Sun Simiao stated: Regularly consuming schisandra in May helps to drain fire from the heart and tonify the large intestine, thereby benefiting the original qi of the five organs.[15p]
    The cold of the bladder has already ceased with the snake (巳), and the kidney's water has ceased with the horse (午). Now, encountering a time of abundant moisture, it assists heat as an evil influence, while the cold from the west and north is completely cleared away. The sage established laws, stating that in summer, what should be supplemented is the true qi of the heavenly origin, not to supplement heat fire, which leads one to consume cold foods in summer. To counteract heat that injures the original qi, ginseng, ophiopogon, and schisandra are used to nourish the pulse. The pulse represents the original qi. The sweetness of ginseng supplements the original qi and drains excessive heat. The bitter coldness of ophiopogon nourishes the source of water and clears dryness that affects the metal (lungs). The sourness of schisandra drains fire while supplementing the large intestine and lung metal. At this time, even those without illness may still exhibit two conditions: either avoiding summer heat by seeking coolness in deep halls and large buildings, which is termed heat stroke.[16p]
    The patient will inevitably experience headaches and chills, a tense and rigid body, aching limbs and joints, and a troubled mind. The skin will be very hot and without sweat, restrained by the cold and dampness of the dwelling, preventing the yang energy from circulating throughout the body. Many in the world use Da Shun San to treat this. If a traveler or farmer works in the heat of midday and becomes afflicted, it is called "zhong re" (heat strike). The symptoms will include severe headaches, dryness and fever, hot skin upon touch, great thirst leading to drinking, profuse sweating, and an inability to move due to a deficiency of qi. This is caused by external heat harming the lung qi, treated with Cang Zhu Bai Hu Tang. Jie Gu states: acquiring this from movement is called "zhong re," while acquiring it from stillness is called "zhong shu" (heat stroke). Zhong shu is an yin condition, needing to be dispersed. Zhong re is a yang condition, resulting from heat harming the original qi, rather than from physical illness. If a person with pre-existing weakness in the spleen and stomach encounters this summer heat, they will surely lose balance, going against natural processes, and will be overcome with fatigue and weakness, speaking little, and having shortness of breath, weak and labored respiratory function, resembling wheezing without being truly wheezing. Their body will feel weak and insubstantial, as if in a dream, hazy like smoke, unaware of their bodily state, accompanied by profuse sweating. This is the loss of essential fluids, and urgent measures should be taken to stop it.[17p]
    Add six pieces of Schisandra, five parts of fried Coptis, and three parts of fried Anemarrhena. Do not let it interfere with eating; adjust according to one's feelings. If it hinders appetite, stop and wait until food is consumed before taking it again. For Sanli and Qijie, draw blood with a three-edged needle; if sweating does not lessen or stop, draw blood three inches below the Sanli point and at the upper edge of the Lian point, and avoid alcohol and damp foods.

    The Qing Shu Yi Qi Decoction treats diseases caused by dietary fatigue that damage the spleen and stomach, exacerbated by summer heat. However, the ingredients that include Ze Xie, Zhu Ling, Fu Ling, Deng Xin, Tong Cao, and Mu Tong, which mildly promote urination, also draw on the excesses of seasonal Qi to relieve the invasions affecting the spleen and stomach, while compensating for the deficiencies of metal and water. This formula has been adjusted accordingly.

    If misapplied to conditions without specific seasonal damp-heat or spleen excess symptoms, or if urination has already increased and the kidneys and liver are not affected, it will surely lead to excessive draining of true Yin, depleting kidney water and first harming the eyes. Therefore, modifications should be made.[18p]
    There is another condition: when the weather is very hot, it can be acquired from labor on the road, or working in the fields; sometimes it occurs in those who are physically weak, eat little, and labor excessively; there are also those who are devoted to good deeds and maintain a constant fast, whose stomach qi has long been deficient, and suffer from this condition due to excessive labor. All these cases resemble the symptoms of internal heat with the Bai Hu Decoction (White Tiger Decoction). There must be strong heat felt in the body upon touching it, as well as irritability and restlessness, extreme heat, thirst leading to excessive drinking of water, and pain seen at the onset of the illness, which is particularly similar to symptoms arising from excessive external heat. If mistakenly treated with Bai Hu Decoction, one would surely die within ten days. This condition indicates a severe deficiency of the spleen and stomach, with insufficient vital energy, shortness of breath through the mouth and nose. After the sun shifts, when the yangming reaches its peak, the illness will surely lessen. If the condition pertains to external heat, by sunset, there will be much more irritability, increased heat, and unrelenting thirst. Those who labor insufficiently do not exhibit these symptoms and are easier to resolve. If there are difficult and ambiguous symptoms, one should wait a day or two before seeking medical treatment, ensuring that mistakes are avoided.[19p]
    Danxi Heart Method (Yuan Dynasty, Zhu Zhenheng)

    Heat Stroke

    For heat stroke, use Huanglian Xiangru drink. If phlegm is present, add Banxia and Nanzhen. For deficiency, add Ginseng and Astragalus. If there is internal injury from heat illness, use Qingshu Yiqi soup. Heat exposure results in phlegm, which should be expelled.

    Heat refers to the intense summer heat; it represents excessive fire energy, which can cause various degrees of damage and injury that can be classified in severity and distinctions between excess and deficiency. Those with abdominal pain and diarrhea may have the stomach and large intestine affected; those with nausea may have phlegm and fluid in the stomach, both being cases of heat exposure, and can use Huanglian Xiangru drink or Qingshu Yiqi soup, as Huanglian clears the heat and Xiangru dispels excess water.

    For those with body heat, headaches, restlessness, or sensations like being pricked by needles, this is due to heat injury in the flesh. One should use Detoxifying soup or Baihu soup with added Chaihu; if there are signs of deficiency, add Ginseng.[20p]
    If one experiences coughing, chills and fever, with persistent night sweats and a rapid pulse, it indicates heat in the lung meridian. Use remedies like Clear Lung Decoction or Chaihu Tianshui Powder for urgent treatment; if delayed, recovery is difficult, leading to the peril of fire overpowering metal, which is a condition of heatstroke. In treating illnesses, one must clearly discern and must not confuse treatments. Such conditions may also occur in spring and autumn; do not adhere rigidly but adjust the prescription according to the illness.

    Dai Sigong says: heatstroke refers to fainting suddenly in summer. It can be caused by fire or phlegm. Fire stems from the two essential fires, while summer heat comes from the two celestial fires; together they create a burning condition, leading to fainting. Phlegm is a bodily fluid that, when heated by summer, gets stirred up and obstructs the heart's passages, causing limbs to lose movement and fainting. Both can be resolved by inducing vomiting. The Inner Classic states: "If fire is stagnant, cause it to be expelled." Vomiting leads to dispersal. Assess the condition's excess or deficiency to induce vomiting, and after recovering consciousness, you may use a clear remedy for treatment.[21p]
    Zhong He

    Zhong He is a condition of excess heat, while heat stroke is a condition of excess cold. If the pulse is weak and deep, cool herbs should not be used. Clearing heat is best achieved with Tian Shui, Wu Ling, or Bai Hu Tang. For heat causing confusion and delirium, use Chen Sha Wu Ling San. If the pulse is wiry and strong, Huang Lian Xiang Ru Tang should be used. If there is severe heat with spontaneous sweating, thirst, and constipation, Wu Ling can be used to promote fluid movement, or Gui Ling Gan Lu Yin. For vomiting and diarrhea with a very weak pulse, Fu Zi Da Shun San can be used. If heat has been injured by cold, Shu Pi Yin or Liang Xiang Yin Zi can both be taken cold. One may also insert garlic cloves into the nostrils or prepare garlic water for irrigation; the potent smell of garlic can open all orifices.[22p]
    On Summer Conditions

    Summer is associated with yin deficiency and insufficient vital energy. At the beginning of summer and the end of spring, symptoms such as headaches, weak limbs, decreased appetite, and a feeling of heat in the body are noted. It is advisable to use the Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang (Rx to tonify the middle and augment the qi) with the removal of Chai Hu and Sheng Ma, adding to it roasted Huang Bo and Bai Shao. For those with phlegm, add Nao Xing, Ban Xia, and Chen Pi for decoction. Alternatively, Sheng Mai Tang (Rx to generate the pulse) may be used. In cases of summer heat combined with phlegm and fire, emetic methods can be employed.

    Discussion on Lurking Yin in Summer Months

    Heaven and Earth operate through a singular vital essence, creating myriad things. The essence rooted in the internal is called "shen ji" (spiritual mechanism), while that rooted externally is referred to as "qi" and "blood." All things share this singular essence. Humans are spiritually connected to these matters; in form, they partake in the cosmos, thus becoming a triad with Heaven and Earth, facilitated by their correct acquisition of qi. Therefore, when qi rises, people also rise, when qi floats, they also float; when qi descends, they descend, and when qi sinks, they also sink. Humanity shares this fundamental key with Heaven and Earth.

    In the first month of the lunar calendar, yin is born, representing the initial movement of yang; in the third month, yang emerges from the earth, marking the ascent of qi. In the sixth month, when yang fully emerges from above, it signifies the floating of qi. The abdomen of a person is connected to the earth's qi, which at this time floats to the skin's surface, leading to a void in the abdomen. The classic text states: "In summer, the meridians are full, the earth’s qi overflows, meridians receive blood, and the skin is filled." During the long summer, qi resides in the muscles, hence the surface is full, and when the surface is full, the interior must be deficient. It is said that in summer, lurking yin resides internally; this notion of yin implies deficiency. To interpret it as simply cold would be a significant misunderstanding.[23p]
    Someone said: By placing the hand on the abdomen, it is clear that it is cold; if not cold, then what is it? Previous scholars treated heat-related illnesses with remedies like Yulong Pills, Dashun Powder, Guiling Pills, boiled ginger with herbs, and other warming formulas. Why does my disciple not contemplate this profoundly? I replied: In spring and summer, we nurture yang; Wang Taibu said that we should eat cool foods in spring and cold foods in summer to nourish yang. This intention is evident. However, places with cool waters, large fans, and cold springs, as well as icy fruits and snow, harm us internally and externally. Without warmth, how can one find peace from illness? Upon careful examination, it is not meant for internal hidden cold. Moreover, ancient sages stated that rising and falling should be followed while cold and heat should be countered. If, in the summer when the fire element is strong, one blindly uses warmth, how can one avoid the real and illusory dangers? Someone else said: The month of Si is purely yang, which may make sense. May has one yin, and June has two yins; is this not cold? I replied: This is the initial movement of yin underground, while four yangs float above ground, scorching and burning like gold melting stone. How can there be any cold? The sage Sun created the Shengmai Powder to be consumed in summer; is this not real?[24p]

    Key Points on Treatment for Heat Stroke

    Heat Stroke

    Heat stroke is characterized by a damp, waxy face and collapse, confusion, and unconsciousness. There is profuse cold sweating and slightly cold extremities. Symptoms may include vomiting, diarrhea, or difficulty breathing. Avoid using cold water or excessively cold substances. A herbal formula can be used to dispel heat, and water can be administered. Alternatively, powdered herbal remedy can be mixed with water, or powdered herbal remedy can be prepared and administered with water. Once the patient shows signs of recovery, give them a warm drink of agastache (香薷) without sediment, adding a small amount of musk for consumption. You may also insert garlic cloves in the nostrils or administer garlic water. The heat and toxins from the heat stroke injure both the exterior and interior. Many heat-relieving medicines contain warming ingredients, such as ginger and cinnamon in the Dashun San, cloves in the Loquat Leaf Powder, and agastache in the agastache drink. Agastache has a spicy and warming nature, as does garlic, which is also strongly pungent and can open all pathways. Generally, extremely pungent and fragrant substances can clear the pathways effectively.[25p]
    When one first feels symptoms of heatstroke, apply a sun-heated tile or cloth soaked in hot broth to the lower abdomen, and urgently administer a decoction of the two qi pills mixed with broth. There was once a guest who suffered from heatstroke, appearing confused, with cold sweat pouring down, limbs cold and lifeless, wanting to throw himself into water, and drooling. This heatstroke was severe, with yin and yang separated, difficult to remedy.

    There is also a milder form of heatstroke, where the person feels drowsy and disinclined to speak. For a robust person, prepare a decoction with fragrant plantain and add one qian of huanglian; for a weak person, use a decoction of star anise and add one qian of fragrant plantain. If after treatment cold sweat continues, limbs remain cold, and there is much thirst and agitation, fragrant plantain decoction should be given. If doctors improperly administer cold remedies, it could lead to persistent vomiting and diarrhea, causing internal coldness and external heat, with increased agitation and thirst, resulting in a desire to be bare, resembling typhoid. In these cases, warming remedies should be used, combining fragrant plantain decoction with fuzi, prepared cold for consumption. For thirst, a decoction of shrinking spleen should be made with fuzi, also prepared cold for consumption.[26p]
    Heat Injury

    Heat injury must be accompanied by sweating, with a cold back and dirty face. Sometimes there is a hot and restless mouth, or headaches and fever, with a marked sense of mental fatigue. This is what is referred to as heat injuring the qi but not the body. However, if the body is not in pain, it differs from the effects of wind or cold. One should take a drink of sweet basil, Liu He soup, or sweet basil soup.

    For those experiencing vomiting and thirst, soaking cold sweet basil soup or taking Wuling powder with summer heat remedy pills is advisable. If vomiting persists, one should use loquat leaf powder with broomcorn root and take the return dan. For vomiting with excessive phlegm, take the summer heat powder with summer heat remedy pills, or Xioa Ban Xia Fu Ling soup, or a summer heat drink.

    For diarrhea and thirst, mix raw Ping Wei powder and raw Wuling powder in equal parts, called Wei Ling Powder; intermittently take the return dan. This dan is not originally a drug for treating diarrhea, but it is suitable for summer heat diarrhea; however, if diarrhea is severe, it should not be used.[27p]
    If there is diarrhea and persistent thirst, one can use spring regulations soup or reduce the spleen drink. When suffering from summer heat with a feeling of heaviness and discomfort in the heart, people often say it is summer poison attacking the heart, not knowing that where there is heat, there is phlegm, and the heaviness and discomfort are caused by phlegm. In the peak of summer heat, if suddenly there is no water and one is extremely thirsty, chewing on green onion about two inches long can replace drinking two liters of water.

    For diarrhea accompanied by abdominal pain with stagnant accumulation, a mixture of fresh five-lichen powder and fragrant qi drink in equal parts can be applied. If there is diarrhea but no accumulation, and the abdominal pain is severe, one can use fresh five-lichen powder with seven parts of musk, or add half a coin of musk to Liuhe soup, or not add musk, just boil the two medicines, strain them, and mix them with Suhexiang pills.

    For those who do not feel thirsty but have dry abdominal pain, boiling Liuhe soup and mixing it with Suhexiang pills is especially appropriate. For diarrhea with fever, use Wei-Ling drink. For diarrhea with thirst, use Wei-Ling drink along with the reduced spleen drink.[28p]
    For symptoms of both thirst and unrelieved heat, take Tanghua Suhexiang pills, swallowing them with restorative pills; or crush restorative pills into a powder and mix with warm water to swallow. For those already relieved, use Xiangru drink. For cases with exterior-induced fever from a cold, use Liuhe Decoction, Xiangru Decoction, or Xiangru drink. If there is body heat and restlessness, use Wuling Powder, or Xiangru Decoction with a pennyweight of Huanglian. If there's heat with profuse sweating and a strong aversion to wind, use raw Wuling Powder. If there's heat and thirst, combine Wuling Powder with Zhi Pizhi drink.

    When summer heat attacks internally causing unresolved heat, with symptoms of restlessness and dry mouth, use Chenshi Wuling Powder, or Xiangru drink with a pennyweight of Huanglian. If there is great thirst that doesn't cease, use Chenshi Wuling Powder, swallowing it with wine boiled with Huanglian pills.

    When summer heat attacks internally, causing stabbing pains in the abdomen and difficulty urinating, use raw Wuling Powder combined with seven parts Mu Xiang.[29p]
    Drinking alcohol in the heat brings summer heat into the intestines. The heat of the alcohol combined with the summer heat leads to fever, intense thirst, and difficult urination, with the urine appearing like blood. Use Wuling San without cinnamon and add a penny of huang lian (coptis). Take Wuling San with the cinnamon and prepare huang lian pills.

    If summer heat enters the stomach causing difficulty in urination, add flavored Xiangru drink and also use Sanhuang pills.

    If summer heat enters the heart, causing body heat and swelling, one should use Chen Sha Wuling San, or add a penny of huang lian to the Xiangru drink.

    For those injured by summer heat and food, symptoms include headache, cold back, spontaneous sweating, fever, aversion to food, nausea, sour odor, and fullness in the chest. Use Liuhe decoction with double the amount of sha ren (galangal seed).

    If due to summer heat one drinks cold food, which leads to internal cold injuries, or has external summer heat injuries, this medicine is also suitable. Summer heat primarily affects the heart, which belongs to the south and fire; the summer heat enters according to its kind.[30p]
    The small intestine is the organ associated with the heart, facilitating the elimination of summer heat toxins through the small intestine. The Five Ling Powder promotes urination and is a treatment for summer heat.

    If one is harmed by summer heat and then exposed to the cold while sleeping, that person may experience symptoms of both summer heat and cold, such as spontaneous sweating, aversion to wind, body aches, and headaches. If they feel cold without clothing yet are restless when dressed, they might already have a fever or not. In either case, it is appropriate to add lotus beans and cardamom to Liu He Decoction. In one formula, use patchouli; in another, use perilla, which is the correct treatment.

    If one has already been affected by summer heat and then further exposed to wind and cold, or suffers from internal cold damage, both patchouli and perilla can release the exterior, while cardamom and lotus beans can warm the interior. However, for those who experience both summer heat and cold without sweating, it is best to use only the aforementioned medicines.[31p]
    If one is affected by the wind, they will inevitably sweat a lot. It is essential to recognize this symptom and to prepare Wuling San, with cinnamon twig as a preferred ingredient. This illness is often prevalent among the common people, frequently occurring when they labor in the heat during the day and sleep with the windows open at night, hoping for coolness. Not covering up leads to unawareness. Those with this condition and experiencing tidal heat, akin to early malaria but not fully developed, should take a mixture of Liuhuo Decoction and Yangwei Decoction in equal parts.

    For those who have this condition and experience a runny nose or a hot feeling coming from the nostrils, they should add half a qian of Chuanxiong to Liuhuo Decoction, along with seven fen each of Qianghuo and Huangqin.

    If one suffers from heat injury and excessively drinks cold water, resulting in summer heat toxins lingering in the chest, leading to clouded consciousness and inability to speak, they should take Xiangru Decoction or Suhexiang Pill.

    For those injured by heat who wash their face with water or bathe, resulting in a clash of summer heat and dampness, causing spontaneous sweating and fever, a feeling of heaviness, and difficulty with urination, Wuling San should be used.[32p]
    If one suffers from heat injury and excessive sweating does not stop, severely leading to the depletion of vital essence, it is advisable to urgently collect the sweat. Use a dosage of Wuling Powder with double the amount of Cinnamon, or add Astragalus equal to the amount of Atractylodes. This is also an ancient method.

    For sweating due to heat injury, along with cold hands and feet, decoct Liuhuo Decoction to mix with Suhexiang Pill.

    If one has sweating due to heat injury, with intermittent twitching of hands and feet, this is known as "heat wind." This occurs because the body has been harmed by heat, causing pores to open, allowing evil wind to invade. It is advisable to use Xiangru Drink or Xiangru Decoction, and one can add one qian of Qianghuo. If phlegm is abundant, use half a dose of Liuhuo Decoction and half a dose of Hexing Xiang San.

    In the hot months, if the body itches like being pricked by needles, with occasional areas of redness and swelling, this is also called "heat wind." For this condition, mix Liuhuo Decoction with Xiaofeng San, taking it with wine. In cases of heat wind combined with vomiting and diarrhea, use half a dose of Liuhuo Decoction and half a dose of Huo Xiang Zheng Qi San, adding three whole scorpions.[33p]
    When summer heat accumulates in the upper body, causing chest fullness and obstruction, and when medicinal soups come back up immediately, preventing passage, there may be symptoms of shortness of breath. One can use Liuhe Decoction steeped in cold water, adding a small amount of musk.

    For those suffering from vexing summer heat with excessive phlegm, in the Xiaoshu Wan, add two qian of Huanglian powder for a formulation known as Huanglian Xiaoshu Wan. Alternatively, one might use Erchen Decoction or Xiao Banxia Fuling Decoction, with an additional one qian of Huanglian.

    If summer heat lingers and causes more severe heat internally and externally, leading to restlessness, spontaneous sweating, and great thirst with a preference for cold, one should take Xiangru Drink with one qian of Huanglian, then follow with Baihu Decoction.

    If the medicinal treatment yields no improvement, it indicates that the summer heat has deeply penetrated, resulting in a build-up of heat inside, characterized by delirium, unrest, thirst, aversion to clothing, constipation, and discolored urine. This should be treated as a heat illness, seeking medication akin to treating febrile diseases, like with the Tiaoguo Chengqi Decoction or Sanhuang Shigao Decoction.

    — Medical Principles by Lou Ying (Ming Dynasty)[34p]
    Heatstroke

    When the pulse is weak, the body is hot, and there is spontaneous sweating accompanied by a dislike of cold, this is known as heatstroke. The prescription is Baihu Decoction with Cinnamon. If one drinks cold beverages first and then suffers from heat, the prescription is Wuling Powder. This is certainly accompanied by a sensation of fullness below the heart. Ginger Decoction should be adjusted for consumption, which is favorable; or one can use the Four Gentleman Decoction for adjustment as well. After achieving balance, if there is difficulty in urination or pain in the lower abdomen, one should use three qian of cattail pollen, five qian of talc, and one qian of gingerly licorice.

    Moreover, regarding the term "Zei Xie" (thieving evil), I said: "The 'Nan Jing' states that there are five evils: real evil, false evil, proper evil, subtle evil, and thieving evil. Those evils that come later are considered false evils; those that come first are considered real evils; those that come from something one cannot overcome are thieving evils; those that come from what one can overcome are subtle evils; and the illness from one's own constitution is the proper evil." Furthermore, for instance, in the case of heart disease, heatstroke is the proper evil, while dampness acquired from it is the thieving evil. Now, if the heart first suffers from heat and dampness overcomes it, water conquering fire is something one cannot withstand, hence it is called thieving evil, which among the five evils is the most contrary. The 'Nan Jing' states that in damp-heat conditions, Yang is moist and weak, and Yin is small and rapid. The weakness appears in the Yang aspect while dampness interacts with heat. The rapid response appears in the Yin aspect while heat steams up the dampness. Therefore, it is stated that heat and dampness act upon each other, termed damp-heat, which is called thieving evil.

    Not only this, I have a chronic issue with stagnant drinking; every time during the hot months, my feet sweat excessively and do not dry. Taking this medicine for two or three doses immediately cures it. For damp-heat with little sweat, Baihu Decoction with Cao Guo; for abundant sweat, Baihu Decoction with Guizhi.[35p]
    Treatment of Summer Heat Disease

    After the summer solstice, diseases caused by heat are termed "summer heat." Summer heat is a manifestation of the rising fire. During the summer months, people are affected by it from the mouth, entering and damaging the heart's protective channels. The pulse may be weak, or either floating and large but scattered, or fine and thin but delayed. This is because the heat damages the qi, leading to its depletion and a weak pulse. Symptoms include sweating, irritability with shortness of breath, excessive talking when calm, body heat with agitation, chest pain, intense thirst, headache accompanied by sweating, fatigue with shortness of breath, or yellowish blood in the stool with rashes; in severe cases, the heat may disturb the heart and spirit, causing loss of consciousness.

    To treat summer heat, it is best to clear the heart and promote urination. Since summer heat damages the qi, augmenting the true qi is crucial. There may also be aversion to cold or cold limbs, and in severe cases, confusion or delirium leading to cholera, vomiting, diarrhea, phlegm causing nausea, or abdominal pain with dysentery; these are not due to summer heat harming the body but rather arise from the body's reaction to summer heat. Because the disease results from summer heat, it is also referred to as summer disease, but the treatment methods differ.

    If a traveler or farmer becomes ill from laboring in the midday sun, it is considered an external injury and a yang condition. Such patients are likely to suffer from severe headaches, agitation, heat intolerance, a hot skin sensation, extreme thirst, sweating with an inability to move, indicating that the hot weather has harmed their original qi. The treatment should focus on clearing summer heat and boosting qi, using herbs such as fragrant rush, coptis, hyacinth bean, ginseng, astragalus, five-flavored herb, anemarrhena, and gypsum.[36p]
    In hot weather, if one experiences thirst and a weak pulse, it is advisable to use the Baihu Decoction with Ginseng. Use 1.5 qian of ginseng, 2 qian each of licorice and anemarrhena, and 5 qian of gypsum. The Zhuyeshigao Decoction is also effective. Use 1 liang of gypsum, 2.5 qian of pinellia, 2 qian each of licorice and ginseng, and 5 qian of ophiopogon, along with bamboo leaves, and boil in water to take.

    If during the hot weather, healthy individuals seek relief from heat and cool themselves in deep halls and cool pavilions with large fans, they attain calmness and experience yin symptoms. This may lead to headaches, chills, stiffness in the body, pain in the limbs and joints, and a feeling of heat without sweating. This is caused by the restraint of yin cold, preventing the yang energy from spreading. It is recommended to use warm and pungent remedies to release the exterior and dispel the cold, using ingredients such as magnolia bark, perilla, dry kudzu, patchouli, notopterygium, and astragalus. If one has already been exposed to cold externally and has also consumed ice water or cold fruits, add dry ginger and cardamom to the previous prescription. This is not to treat heat directly but to address the diseases caused by heat.

    If there is no external cold exposure and the issue is simply due to internal injury from cold water or cold items, resulting in abdominal pain or diarrhea, or cholera with vomiting, it is advisable to use the Suoping Decoction. Ingredients include cardamom, wild cardamom, licorice, lentils, dry ginger, and black plum; or modify the Lior Zhong Decoction by adding shenkui, malt, cardamom, and astragalus. This specifically treats internal issues, warming the center and aiding digestion.[37p]
    If there are severe symptoms of diarrhea and the pulse is deep and very weak, do not use cooling medicines; instead, use the Fuzi Dazhun Powder, which consists of roasted Fuzi, licorice, dried ginger, apricot kernel, and cinnamon. Alternatively, you can use the Fuzi Lizhong Decoction with added peony root.

    (Note: According to Danxi, the cycles of heaven and earth reflect the changing of the five elements, leading to the four seasons; likewise, the five organs and six bowels of humans also follow this pattern. April corresponds to the Fire of the Snake, and May corresponds to the Fire of the Horse, which is overly strong; Fire is the husband of Metal (Lung), thus an excess of Fire leads to a decline of Metal. June corresponds to the Earth of the Sheep, which is too strong; Earth is the husband of Water (Kidney), thus an excess of Earth leads to a decline of Water. Moreover, the Kidney Water often relies on the Lung Metal for nurturing to compensate for its deficiencies. In ancient times, during the summer months, people would sleep alone and eat bland foods to nurture the organs of Metal and Water. The classics state: "He who stores essence in winter does not suffer from warmth in spring." October corresponds to the Water of the Pig, and November corresponds to the Water of the Rat, when the Fire energy is stored; one must nurture the foundational truth to support the emergence of spring. If during this time one does not indulge in desires and harm oneself, by the time spring arrives, one will be robust and strong, and what illness can one speak of?)

    If in the summer there is damage from heat leading to fever, excessive sweating, and loss of strength, where the pulse is weak, thin, and slow, this indicates heat damaging the vital energy. The prescription includes ginseng, honey-fried astragalus, fried lily, white peony root, aged tangerine peel, white poria (each 3 grams), fried yellow jían (2.5 grams), and three grams of berberine, 1.5 grams of white atractylodes, 7 grams of fragrant flat-leaved mint and anemone (mothers of wisdom); decocting with ginger water, to be taken warm before meals.[38p]
    Note: Regarding the previous cases, there are those with heat injuring the vital energy causing sweating, those with overexertion injuring the vital energy also causing sweating, and those with pre-existing weakness of the vital energy leading to profuse sweating due to loose pores. Treatment methods: For heat injuring the vital energy, use Qing Shu Yi Qi Decoction; for overexertion injuring the vital energy, use Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction; for pre-existing weakness of the vital energy with spontaneous sweating, use Shi Quan Da Bu Decoction. If there is also night sweats, add Liu Wei Wan with Wu Wei Zi. Previously mentioned large sweating with weakness, pulse weak, thin, and slow, pertains to deficiency of yang qi. Internally, Huang Lian and Zhi Mu may further injure yang qi, while Shao Yao and Fu Ling may harm yin qi, so the practitioner must differentiate accordingly.

    In cases of summer and autumn heat, due to excessive consumption of cold substances like tea and water that injure the insides, combined with overexposure to cold air that injures the outsides, leading to chills and fever, fullness and oppression in the chest, and poor appetite, possibly with symptoms of vomiting and diarrhea, this is a case of injury from both internal and external cold. The prescription is: Ren Shen, Gan Jiang (stir-fried to purple), Hou Po (stir-fried), Chen Pi, Qiang Huo, Zhi Shi, Bai Fu Ling each 3 grams, Bai Zhu 4.5 grams, Honey-fried Gan Cao 1.5 grams, decoct with ginger water and take warm before meals.

    Note: For the previously described case, this formula should be used. If it does not respond, Huo Xiang Zheng Qi San should be used. If both internal and external cold are resolved but the fever and chills have not subsided, or if appetite remains poor, use Liu Jun Zi Decoction. The "Bao Ming Ji" states: For cholera belonging to the Yang Ming pattern, use combinations like He Zhong, Ping Wei, Jian Zhong Decoction, or Si Jun Zi Decoction.[39p]
    When the pulse is floating with spontaneous sweating, add cinnamon twig to the Four Gentlemen formula. If the pulse is floating without sweating, add ephedra. If there is vomiting or loose stools with cramping, and pain on the sides with a wiry pulse, it indicates wood overcoming earth; use Pingwei Powder with papaya, or Jianzhong Decoction with bupleurum and papaya. If there are vomiting, loose stools, abdominal pain, and body heaviness, with a submerged and thin pulse, add white peony and galangal to the Four Gentlemen formula. For vomiting and loose stools with stiffness in the limbs, a submerged and slow pulse belongs to the lesser yin condition; add ginger, aconite, and magnolia bark to the Four Gentlemen formula. For vomiting and loose stools with coldness in the limbs and a faint and slow pulse indicating the jueyin condition, add angelica and aconite to Jianzhong Decoction. If vomiting and a headache with body heat occur, and there is much thirst, use Wuling Powder. If there is coldness and aversion to water, treat with Lizhong Pill. The "Yuanrong" states that for a taiyin condition with cholera, add dried tangerine peel to Lizhong. For vomiting, lower abdominal pain, and coldness in the hands and feet, add熟 aconite to Lizhong. If cramping occurs after vomiting and diarrhea, add fire-roasted gypsum to Lizhong.

    If summer heat is encountered during travel, regularly consume to strengthen vital energy, clear heat, and dispel summer heat to prevent heat stroke, cholera, diarrhea, dysentery, and other conditions. The formula consists of 1.2 grams of ginseng, 1.5 grams of atractylodes, ten crushed schisandra berries, 2 grams each of ophiopogon (without the heart), fried white peony, and white poria, 0.7 grams each of fried anemarrhena, dried tangerine peel, and fragrant madder, 0.3 grams of fried yellow gip, and 0.5 grams of honey-fried licorice, boiled with ginger water and taken warm before meals.[40p]
    Note: According to previous evidence, if a person's vital energy is weak, it is advisable to use a formula for tonifying energy, removing Chai Hu and Sheng Ma, and adding Mai Men Dong and Wu Wei Zi, or a small amount of fried black Huang Bo; Ren Shen Yi Qi Tang can also be employed. If one encounters fatigue and has overexerted themselves, taking two or three doses of the following formula can prevent internal injuries and fever. This formula focuses on tonifying energy. The ingredients include one and a half qian of honey-fried Huang Qi, one qian each of Ren Shen, Mai Men Dong (with the heart removed), and Chen Pi, one qian of Bai Zhu, seven fen of fried Gan Cao, decocted in ginger and jujube water, to be taken warm before meals. If fatigued severely, add four or five fen of cooked Fu Zi.

    Note: According to previous discussions on revealing the ignorance of the secular world and alleviating endless sufferings. Internally using Fu Zi is especially suitable for those who are typically sensitive to cold food and drink. If someone generally likes cold food and drink, it is also acceptable to substitute with meat桂 (Rou Gui) or fried ginger. If the fatigue is caused by heat injuring energy, leading to tired limbs or numbness in hands and feet, one should first use Ren Shen Yi Qi Tang and then use Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang.

    If a person has overworked their mind with worry, damaging their spirit, experiencing dizziness and blurred vision, with weak heart and shortness of breath, one should primarily tonify blood. The formula includes one qian of Ren Shen, fifteen grains of Wu Wei Zi pounded, one qian each of fried Bai Shao, fried Suan Zao Ren, Fu Shen (with the heart removed), and cured Dang Gui, and five fen each of Gan Cao, Chen Pi, Chuan Xiong, Shao Di Huang (washed with wine), fried Shan Zhi Zi, and Mai Men Dong (with the heart removed), which are to be decocted in water and taken.[41p]
    Note: The previous diagnosis should use this formula and should not be taken in excess. Ingredients such as Ophiopogon (Mai Men Dong), Peony (Shao Yao), Gardenia (Shan Zhi), and Rehmannia (Sheng Di) are bitter and cold, which may further harm the spleen's qi. If the spleen and stomach are generally weak and hot and one suffers from the previous symptoms, it is enough to use the "Buzhong Yiqi Decoction" with Ophiopogon and Five-Flavored Herb. If due to hunger, thirst, or overexertion, leading to high qi and panting, a hot body and agitation, or spontaneous sweating, this indicates internal injury to the yang qi, and the "Buzhong Yiqi Decoction" should be used. If due to fluctuations in hunger and fullness or improper sweating, resulting in hot, dry muscles, intense thirst, red eyes, flushed face, a large pulse that feels vacuous upon pressing, this indicates blood loss and agitation, and the "Danggui Buxue Decoction" should be used.

    Heat resulting from summer heat is due to fire evil harming the heart, consuming the original qi, and causing the evil heat to invade. Thus, it results in excessive sweating, lack of strength, and a weak, slow pulse, which is the external heat evil harming the nourishment and should be treated internally.

    Note: In summer, yang qi is predominant externally while yin qi is hidden internally. The principle should be to primarily tonify the yang qi while simultaneously alleviating heat, following the good method of the "Inner Canon" of addressing time in accordance with indications. Therefore, in the previous case, one should investigate the cause and treat it accordingly; the indiscriminate use of herbs like Pogostemon (Xiangru) decoction should be avoided, as it can scatter the yang qi, damage the true yin, and worsen the condition.[42p]
    In summer, people use mint to brew tea, not realizing that it disperses one's true vitality, similar to how prolonged use of Chuanxiong soup can lead to sudden death.

    Summer ailments caused by heat, although categorized as external influences, are akin to internal injuries and are significantly different from those of cold damage. Cold harms the exterior and obstructs the surface, presenting signs of excess, thus requiring sweating. Heat injures the vital energy, dissipating it and showing signs of deficiency, hence it needs to be replenished. This is what Dongyuan referred to as "clearing heat and benefiting energy."

    There are also cases where excessive consumption of cold substances due to the heat might harm the internal organs, or overexposure to cold air might damage the exterior; these are not injuries from heat but rather sicknesses caused by oneself due to the heat, and should be treated with warming and dispersing herbs or warming herbs that regulate the interior, similar to treatments for cold damage.

    During summer, the yang energy rises to the surface, while yin energy sinks within. Overexertion through diet or labor can internally harm the qi, or excessive labor in intense heat can harm the yang energy, leading to numerous ailments. The principle should be to primarily tonify the original qi, supplemented by treatments that dispel heat. If one suffers from heat stroke, it indicates a deficiency of yin-cold, and the principle should be to primarily tonify the yang energy, with a slight addition of heat-dispelling treatments. Therefore, many ancient sages often used ginger, cinnamon, and aconite; this follows the sound principle of the "Inner Canon" of treating based on symptoms rather than time.

    Today, when faced with heat symptoms resulting in blue or darkened extremities or body parts, this is often due to not understanding the cause or inadequately warming and tonifying the interior, instead relying on the indiscriminate use of fragrant herbs like Banlangen tea. Banlangen tea disperses yang energy and leads the true yin, and if one’s vital energy is already weak or if there has been excessive labor and they use it, it is rarely without danger.[43p]

    Introduction to Medicine (Ming Dynasty, Li Zhan)

    Distinguishing Between Deficiency and Excess, Yin and Yang

    For summer diseases, when the body is hot with spontaneous sweating, thirst, and a dirty face, other symptoms are secondary changes that may involve internal injury. One must first inquire if the person has a history of deficiency or a weak stomach, or if they suffered from a major illness or exhaustive effort that led to summer heat injury; in such cases, it is advisable to clear summer heat and bolster energy.

    If the person is fundamentally strong, robust, and without any signs of deficiency or illness, it is advisable to dispel summer heat and harmonize the middle.

    For those residing in high, spacious buildings, if they suffer from what appears to be a heat syndrome related to the heart and spleen meridians, it is termed heatstroke, a yin condition; while those engaged in outdoor activities, experiencing symptoms similar to a cold syndrome related to the bladder meridian, it is termed sunstroke, which is a yang condition; yet in essence, they are the same.

    However, when discussing heat exposure, it is referred to as heatstroke, whereas when referring to being pressured by the sun, it is called sunstroke. At the onset of heat, it enters through the mouth, nose, teeth, and cheeks, reaching the palms, thereby producing heat from heat. Hence, ancient methods to dispel summer heat include using cool water for irrigation, though it should not be swallowed. When it enters the liver, it causes dizziness and stiffness; when it enters the spleen, it results in faintness and unawareness; when it enters the lungs, it leads to cough, wheezing, and debilitation; and when it enters the kidneys, it causes excessive thirst, not limited to affecting the heart but impacting multiple organs as well.[44p]
    Distinguishing Heatstroke and Heat Invasion

    Heatstroke brings the heart to a lethargic state, leading to fainting. Heat injury affects the flesh, causing restlessness throughout the body, which may feel like being pricked by needles or experiencing redness and swelling. This occurs because the heat rises above the ground, causing the body's energy to also rise to the surface of the skin.

    When heat invades the stomach and intestines, it results in abdominal pain, nausea, vomiting, and diarrhea. "Hidden heat" refers to heat that has invaded for a long duration and becomes concealed within the three burners of the stomach and intestines, damaging the vital energy without harming the form. Over a period of weeks or months, it may lead to fluctuating cold and heat, resulting in symptoms such as cholera, vomiting, diarrhea, bloating, intermittent fevers, thirst, abdominal pain, and blood in the stool. However, heat illness often does not involve body pain; if pain does occur, it is likely due to bathing, where moistness and heat conflict.[45p]
    Distinguishing Wind from Syncope

    This refers to the occurrence of heat in the middle and the indication of wind by the twitching of hands and feet, while coldness in the extremities points to syncope. Syncope and the hot syncope from cold damage have similar meanings; one might use Huanglian Xiangru San. Summer wind arises from overexertion, stirring the fire within the five organs, which, when combined with external heat, causes the metal to weaken and wood to flourish, leading to the generation of wind. In this case, Xiangru San may be combined with Qianghuo, or Liuhe Decoction combined with Xiaofeng San. If there is already phlegm and fluids present, and summer heat causes agitation, the combination of Liuhe Decoction and Xingxiang San should be applied.

    If a person suddenly collapses on the road and it is not convenient to administer medicine, fearing loss of energy may result in difficulty in treatment, one should urgently support them in a cool place, avoiding damp and cold ground. Heat from the road should be drawn away by placing warm earth on the navel and making openings, encouraging urination over it. Fresh ginger or garlic should be chewed and taken with hot soup or children's urine. Externally, apply a cloth dipped in hot soup to warm the Qi Hai point, encouraging recovery.

    It is particularly important afterward not to drink cold water, but instead take large doses of restorative medicine. For confusion of mind, Wuling San may be used, boiled with lamb's heart and mixed with powdered cinnabar for oral intake. If sweating occurs, add Huangqi. If someone has been drinking alcohol and heat enters the stomach causing blood in the urine, remove the cinnamon and add Huanglian. If there is confusion, palpitations, and nonsensical speech, use Yiyuan San with an increased amount of cinnabar, mixed with freshly drawn water for dosage. This is essential medicine to lower stomach fire, treat agitation, resolve dampness, and quell thirst.[46p]
    Heat Toxin and Phlegm Fire

    Heat toxin and phlegm fire can obstruct the chest, requiring an assessment of the body's condition to expel it, signifying that pent-up fire can be released. If there is phlegm, wheezing, shortness of breath, and a feeling of fullness in the chest, and medicines cannot be ingested, urgently prepare Liuhe Decoction blended with two厘 of musk to take.

    Treatment Method
    In summer, people often drink cold water and eat cold food, thus promoting dampness while also aiding in dispersal and transport. For those who sweat excessively, it is advisable to avoid diuretics. To dispel heat, the following are recommended: Xiangru San, Huanglian Jiedu Decoction, Qingfei Shengmai San, and Baihu Decoction with ginseng and chuanxiong added. If there is irregular cold and heat, use Xiao Chaihu Decoction. For harmonizing, it is suitable to use Xiao and Da Jiaozhong Decoction, Ruzhu Ling Decoction, Pi Pa Ye San, Weiling Decoction, Gui Ling Ganlu Drink, and Liuhe Decoction.

    When there is hidden dampness inside, avoiding heat and craving coolness, while also being assailed by cold air from outside can depress the body's yang energy; therefore, it is appropriate to resolve this with spicy and warm dispersing remedies like Xianghuo Decoction. If there is exterior cold already received, and internally cold injury occurs, add dried ginger, cardamom, and shenqu. Conversely, if one is exposed to heat from the outside while sustaining internal injuries from cold food, leading to exterior heat and internal cold, use Qing Shu Yiqi Decoction. If there is no external cold but merely internal injury from cold causes abdominal pain and diarrhea, utilize Lizhong Decoction with malt and cardamom; or Da Shun San, or Erqi Dan with cold water; all serve to treat this condition. Inducing heat injury from cold is different from warming and dispersing to treat summer heat. Mistaken consumption can cause jaundice, spotting, accumulation of blood, distress, and death.[47p]
    For those suffering internal injuries from labor, or who are inherently weak with deficient qi and blood, particularly in the heat of summer, the primary focus should be on nourishment, and one must be cautious with the use of extremely hot or cold remedies. For those heavily affected by the heat with dark urine, the "Qing Shu Yi Qi Decoction" is recommended. For those with mild heat and fatigue, the "Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction" or even pills may be used. During temporary heatstroke, add fragrant plants like "Xiang Ru" and "Bian Dou". If there is yin deficiency, "Zi Yin Jiang Huo Decoction" or "Shen Qi Pill" should be administered.

    Severe heat damages qi. Health practitioners state that indulging in drinking and lust during this season can lead to the internal decay of the kidneys, ultimately resulting in deterioration by autumn and, in severe cases, leading to death by water retention. Regular protection against heat is advised; for those with a strong constitution, "Xiang Ru San" or "Yi Yuan San" may be used, while those with deficiencies should avoid it. It is known that individuals with spleen deficiency need not be overly troubled by summer labor or exposure to cool conditions; they often find themselves with headaches, weakness in the legs, little appetite, and a warm body at the turn of spring to early summer, a condition termed summer illness. The "Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction" is suitable, omitting "Sheng" and "Chai," as well as ingredients like "Huang Bo," "Shao Yao," "Wu Wei," and "Mai Dong." If there is phlegm, add "Ban Xia" and ginger juice. This serves as a sacred remedy for eliminating summer heat.

    For those experiencing fatigue, inadequate spirit, thirst, and loss of appetite, "Sheng Mai San" or "Yao Xing Wan," and universally "Xie Fu Wan Bing Wu You San" are suggested for their efficacy.[48p]
    Heat Stroke

    Heat is a manifestation of the upward movement of fire. In the summer months, when people are exposed to it, it enters through the mouth and teeth, damaging the heart meridians and collaterals. The pulse may be weak, or it can be floating and large, or stringy, thin, weak, and slow. When heat injures the Qi, the Qi diminishes, leading to a weak pulse. The external symptoms include headache, body heat, dry mouth, thirst, facial greasiness, spontaneous sweating, fatigue, shortness of breath, chills, and aversion to heat. In severe cases, there may be delirium, resulting in cholera, vomiting, diarrhea, phlegm, and inverted flow, alongside yellowing and spots on the skin, all indicative of this condition. In more severe cases, the excess fire overwhelms metal, failing to balance wood, leading to liver excess and convulsions, resulting in a loss of consciousness. The pulse is weak and floating; the floating represents wind and the weak represents summer heat, commonly referred to as summer wind. The recommended treatment is a formula of Huang Lian and Xiang Ru decoction with added Qiang Huo, or simply a Shuang Jie powder with added Xiang Ru.[49p]
    Generally, the method for treating summer heat should focus on clearing the heart and promoting urination. If there is excessive sweating, one should not promote urination but instead use Bai Hu Tang to clear the heat. Next, treat the exterior and interior accordingly. If it is an exterior condition with headache and aversion to cold, one should use formulas like Shuang Jie San, adding Xiang Ru, or the Ten Flavor Xiang Ru Drink.
